  </div>\n   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Cosmic ray\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       "Cosmic radiation" redirects here. For some other types of cosmic radiation, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_background_radiation" title="Cosmic background radiation">\n        cosmic background radiation\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Cosmic_background_(disambiguation)" title="Cosmic background (disambiguation)">\n        cosmic background (disambiguation)\n       </a>\n       . For the film, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_Ray_(film)" title="Cosmic Ray (film)">\n        Cosmic Ray (film)\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="400" height="432" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg/360px-Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg/540px-Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg/720px-Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg.png 2x" width="360"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cosmic_ray_flux_versus_particle_energy.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cosmic flux versus particle energy\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:82px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Air_shower_detected_in_a_cloud_chamber.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="80" data-file-width="80" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Air_shower_detected_in_a_cloud_chamber.jpg" width="80"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Air_shower_detected_in_a_cloud_chamber.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Air shower detected in a\n         <a href="/wiki/Cloud_chamber" title="Cloud chamber">\n          cloud chamber\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Cosmic rays\n       </b>\n       are\n       <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">\n        high-energy radiation\n       </a>\n       , mainly originating outside the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">\n        Solar System\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and even from distant galaxies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Upon impact with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth\'s atmosphere">\n        Earth\'s atmosphere\n       </a>\n       , cosmic rays can produce\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_shower_(physics)" title="Air shower (physics)">\n        showers of secondary particles\n       </a>\n       that sometimes reach the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_surface" title="Earth\'s surface">\n        surface\n       </a>\n       . Composed primarily of high-energy\n       <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">\n        protons\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_nuclei" title="Atomic nuclei">\n        atomic nuclei\n       </a>\n       , they are of mysterious origin. Data from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fermi_Gamma-ray_Space_Telescope" title="Fermi Gamma-ray Space Telescope">\n        Fermi Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       (2013)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ackermann-2013_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ackermann-2013-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       have been interpreted as evidence that a significant fraction of primary cosmic rays originate from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">\n        supernova\n       </a>\n       explosions of stars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinholster-2013_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pinholster-2013-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_galactic_nuclei" title="Active galactic nuclei">\n        Active galactic nuclei\n       </a>\n       probably also produce cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nature_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nature-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Etymology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Energy_distribution">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Energy distribution\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Types">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Types\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#Primary_cosmic_rays">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Primary cosmic rays\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3           Primary cosmic ray antimatter\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a 9.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Significance to aerospace travel\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 lightning\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#Postulated_role_in_climate_change">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Postulated role in climate change\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#Research_and_experiments">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Research and experiments\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24">\n           <a href="#Ground-based">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Ground-based\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Satellite">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Satellite\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Balloon-borne">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Balloon-borne\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#Further_references">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further references\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The term\n       <i>\n        ray\n       </i>\n       is a historical accident, as cosmic rays were at first, and wrongly, thought to be mostly\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">\n        electromagnetic radiation\n       </a>\n       . In common scientific usage,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       high-energy particles with intrinsic mass are known as "cosmic" rays, while\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photons" title="Photons">\n        photons\n       </a>\n       , which are quanta of electromagnetic radiation (and so have no intrinsic mass) are known by their common names, such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n         gamma rays\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       or\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">\n         X-rays\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , depending on their\n       <a href="/wiki/Photon_energy" title="Photon energy">\n        photon energy\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Massive_cosmic_rays_compared_to_photons">\n        Massive cosmic rays compared to photons\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Massive cosmic rays compared to photons">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In current usage, the term\n       <i>\n        cosmic ray\n       </i>\n       almost exclusively refers to\n       <a href="/wiki/Massive_particle" title="Massive particle">\n        massive particles\n       </a>\n       , as opposed to\n       <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">\n        photons\n       </a>\n       . Massive particles \xe2\x80\x93 those that have\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_mass" title="Rest mass">\n        rest mass\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 gain additional,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">\n        kinetic\n       </a>\n       , mass-energy when they are moving, due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass_in_special_relativity" title="Mass in special relativity">\n        relativistic effects\n       </a>\n       . Through this process, some particles acquire tremendously high mass-energies. These are significantly higher than the\n       <a href="/wiki/Photon_energy" title="Photon energy">\n        photon energy\n       </a>\n       of even the highest-energy photons detected to date. The energy of the massless photon depends solely on\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_spectrum" title="Electromagnetic spectrum">\n        frequency\n       </a>\n       , not speed, as photons always travel at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">\n        same speed\n       </a>\n       . At the higher end of the energy spectrum, relativistic kinetic energy is the main source of the mass-energy of cosmic rays.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Oh-My-God_particle" title="Oh-My-God particle">\n        Oh-My-God particle\n       </a>\n       , the highest-energy\n       <a href="/wiki/Fermion" title="Fermion">\n        fermionic\n       </a>\n       cosmic ray detected to date, had an energy of about\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n         7020300000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n        </span>\n        3\n        <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n         \xc3\x97\n        </span>\n        10\n        <sup>\n         20\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Electronvolt" title="Electronvolt">\n         eV\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       , while the highest-energy gamma rays to be observed,\n       <a href="/wiki/Very-high-energy_gamma_ray" title="Very-high-energy gamma ray">\n        very-high-energy gamma rays\n       </a>\n       , are photons with energies of up to\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n         6995160217648700000\xe2\x99\xa0\n        </span>\n        10\n        <sup>\n         14\n        </sup>\n        eV\n       </span>\n       . Hence, the highest-energy detected fermionic cosmic ray was around\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n         7006300000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n        </span>\n        3\n        <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n         \xc3\x97\n        </span>\n        10\n        <sup>\n         6\n        </sup>\n       </span>\n       times more energetic than the highest-energy detected cosmic photons.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">\n        Composition\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Of primary cosmic rays, which originate outside of Earth\'s atmosphere, about 99% are the nuclei of well-known atoms (stripped of their electron shells), and about 1% are solitary electrons (similar to\n       <a href="/wiki/Beta_particle" title="Beta particle">\n        beta particles\n       </a>\n       ). Of the nuclei, about 90% are simple\n       <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">\n        protons\n       </a>\n       (i.e., hydrogen nuclei); 9% are\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_particle" title="Alpha particle">\n        alpha particles\n       </a>\n       , identical to helium nuclei; and 1% are the nuclei of heavier elements, called\n       <a href="/wiki/HZE_ions" title="HZE ions">\n        HZE ions\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goddard-2012_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-goddard-2012-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A very small fraction are stable particles of\n       <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">\n        antimatter\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Antiproton" title="Antiproton">\n        antiprotons\n       </a>\n       . The precise nature of this remaining fraction is an area of active research. An active search from Earth orbit for anti-alpha particles has failed to detect them.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">\n        Energy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Energy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays attract great interest practically, due to the damage they inflict on microelectronics and life outside the protection of an atmosphere and magnetic field, and scientifically, because the energies of the most energetic\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultra-high-energy_cosmic_ray" title="Ultra-high-energy cosmic ray">\n        ultra-high-energy cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       (UHECRs) have been observed to approach\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        3 \xc3\x97 10\n        <sup>\n         20\n        </sup>\n        eV\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nerlich-2011_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nerlich-2011-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       about 40 million times the energy of particles accelerated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">\n        Large Hadron Collider\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lhc1-cern_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lhc1-cern-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One can show that such enormous energies might be achieved by means of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Centrifugal_mechanism_of_acceleration" title="Centrifugal mechanism of acceleration">\n        centrifugal mechanism of acceleration\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_galactic_nuclei" title="Active galactic nuclei">\n        active galactic nuclei\n       </a>\n       . At 50\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       J,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gaensler-2013_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gaensler-2013-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the highest-energy ultra-high-energy cosmic rays have energies comparable to the kinetic energy of a 90-kilometre-per-hour (56\xc2\xa0mph) baseball. As a result of these discoveries, there has been interest in investigating cosmic rays of even greater energies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Most cosmic rays, however, do not have such extreme energies; the energy distribution of cosmic rays peaks at 0.3 gigaelectronvolts (4.8\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x9211\n       </sup>\n       J).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hyperphysics-2012_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hyperphysics-2012-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       After the discovery of\n       <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_decay" title="Radioactive decay">\n        radioactivity\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Henri_Becquerel" title="Henri Becquerel">\n        Henri Becquerel\n       </a>\n       in 1896, it was generally believed that atmospheric electricity,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ionization" title="Ionization">\n        ionization\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth\'s atmosphere">\n        air\n       </a>\n       , was caused only by\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n        radiation\n       </a>\n       from radioactive elements in the ground or the radioactive gases or isotopes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Radon" title="Radon">\n        radon\n       </a>\n       they produce.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malley2011_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Malley2011-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Measurements of ionization rates at increasing heights above the ground during the decade from 1900 to 1910 showed a decrease that could be explained as due to absorption of the ionizing radiation by the intervening air.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-North2008_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-North2008-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery">\n        Discovery\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Discovery">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 1909,\n       <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Wulf" title="Theodor Wulf">\n        Theodor Wulf\n       </a>\n       developed an\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrometer" title="Electrometer">\n        electrometer\n       </a>\n       , a device to measure the rate of ion production inside a hermetically sealed container, and used it to show higher levels of radiation at the top of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">\n        Eiffel Tower\n       </a>\n       than at its base. However, his paper published in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Physikalische_Zeitschrift" title="Physikalische Zeitschrift">\n         Physikalische Zeitschrift\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was not widely accepted. In 1911,\n       <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Pacini" title="Domenico Pacini">\n        Domenico Pacini\n       </a>\n       observed simultaneous variations of the rate of ionization over a lake, over the sea, and at a depth of 3 meters from the surface. Pacini concluded from the decrease of radioactivity underwater that a certain part of the ionization must be due to sources other than the radioactivity of the Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacini_measurement.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="997" data-file-width="1375" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pacini_measurement.jpg/160px-Pacini_measurement.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pacini_measurement.jpg/240px-Pacini_measurement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pacini_measurement.jpg/320px-Pacini_measurement.jpg 2x" width="160"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacini_measurement.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Pacini makes a measurement in 1910.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1912,\n       <a href="/wiki/Victor_Francis_Hess" title="Victor Francis Hess">\n        Victor Hess\n       </a>\n       carried three enhanced-accuracy Wulf electrometers\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HessNobelPresSp_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HessNobelPresSp-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to an altitude of 5300 meters in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Hot_air_balloon" title="Hot air balloon">\n        free balloon\n       </a>\n       flight. He found the ionization rate increased approximately fourfold over the rate at ground level.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HessNobelPresSp_16-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HessNobelPresSp-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hess ruled out the Sun as the radiation\'s source by making a balloon ascent during a near-total eclipse. With the moon blocking much of the Sun\'s visible radiation, Hess still measured rising radiation at rising altitudes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HessNobelPresSp_16-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HessNobelPresSp-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He concluded "The results of my observation are best explained by the assumption that a radiation of very great penetrating power enters our atmosphere from above." In 1913\xe2\x80\x931914,\n       <a href="/wiki/Werner_Kolh%C3%B6rster" title="Werner Kolh\xc3\xb6rster">\n        Werner Kolh\xc3\xb6rster\n       </a>\n       confirmed Victor Hess\' earlier results by measuring the increased ionization rate at an altitude of 9\xc2\xa0km.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HessKol.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="720" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/HessKol.jpg/220px-HessKol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/HessKol.jpg/330px-HessKol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/HessKol.jpg/440px-HessKol.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HessKol.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Increase of ionization with altitude as measured by Hess in 1912 (left) and by Kolh\xc3\xb6rster (right)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Hess received the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">\n        Nobel Prize in Physics\n       </a>\n       in 1936 for his discovery.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Hess balloon flight took place on 7 August 1912. By sheer coincidence, exactly 100 years later on 7 August 2012, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n        Mars Science Laboratory\n       </a>\n       rover used its\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">\n        Radiation Assessment Detector\n       </a>\n       (RAD) instrument to begin measuring the radiation levels on another planet for the first time. On 31 May 2013, NASA scientists reported that a possible\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manned_mission_to_Mars" title="Manned mission to Mars">\n        manned mission to Mars\n       </a>\n       may involve a greater\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n        radiation risk\n       </a>\n       than previously believed, based on the amount of\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n        energetic particle radiation\n       </a>\n       detected by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">\n        RAD\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n        Mars Science Laboratory\n       </a>\n       while traveling from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       in 2011\xe2\x80\x932012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531a_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531a-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531b_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531b-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130530_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130530-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hessballon.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1018" data-file-width="876" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Hessballon.jpg/220px-Hessballon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Hessballon.jpg/330px-Hessballon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Hessballon.jpg/440px-Hessballon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hessballon.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Hess lands after his balloon flight in 1912.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Identification">\n        Identification\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Identification">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Rossi" title="Bruno Rossi">\n        Bruno Rossi\n       </a>\n       wrote that:\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the late 1920s and early 1930s the technique of self-recording electroscopes carried by balloons into the highest layers of the atmosphere or sunk to great depths under water was brought to an unprecedented degree of perfection by the German physicist\n       <a href="/wiki/Erich_Regener" title="Erich Regener">\n        Erich Regener\n       </a>\n       and his group. To these scientists we owe some of the most accurate measurements ever made of cosmic-ray ionization as a function of altitude and depth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">\n        Ernest Rutherford\n       </a>\n       stated in 1931 that "thanks to the fine experiments of Professor Millikan and the even more far-reaching experiments of Professor Regener, we have now got for the first time, a curve of absorption of these radiations in water which we may safely rely upon".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1920s, the term\n       <i>\n        cosmic rays\n       </i>\n       was coined by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Millikan" title="Robert Millikan">\n        Robert Millikan\n       </a>\n       who made measurements of ionization due to cosmic rays from deep under water to high altitudes and around the globe. Millikan believed that his measurements proved that the primary cosmic rays were gamma rays; i.e., energetic photons. And he proposed a theory that they were produced in interstellar space as by-products of the fusion of hydrogen atoms into the heavier elements, and that secondary\n       <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">\n        electrons\n       </a>\n       were produced in the atmosphere by\n       <a href="/wiki/Compton_scattering" title="Compton scattering">\n        Compton scattering\n       </a>\n       of gamma rays. But then, sailing from\n       <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">\n        Java\n       </a>\n       to the Netherlands in 1927,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Clay" title="Jacob Clay">\n        Jacob Clay\n       </a>\n       found evidence,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clay-1927_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-clay-1927-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       later confirmed in many experiments, of a variation of cosmic ray intensity with latitude, which indicated that the primary cosmic rays are deflected by the geomagnetic field and must therefore be charged particles, not photons. In 1929,\n       <a href="/wiki/Walther_Bothe" title="Walther Bothe">\n        Bothe\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Werner_Kolh%C3%B6rster" title="Werner Kolh\xc3\xb6rster">\n        Kolh\xc3\xb6rster\n       </a>\n       discovered charged cosmic-ray particles that could penetrate 4.1\xc2\xa0cm of gold.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bothe-korlhorster-1929_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bothe-korlhorster-1929-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Charged particles of such high energy could not possibly be produced by photons from Millikan\'s proposed interstellar fusion process.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1930,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Rossi" title="Bruno Rossi">\n        Bruno Rossi\n       </a>\n       predicted a difference between the intensities of cosmic rays arriving from the east and the west that depends upon the charge of the primary particles \xe2\x80\x93 the so-called "east-west effect."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rossi-1930_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rossi-1930-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Three independent experiments\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-johnson-1933_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-johnson-1933-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alvarez-compton-1933_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-alvarez-compton-1933-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rossi-1934_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rossi-1934-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       found that the intensity is, in fact, greater from the west, proving that most primaries are positive. During the years from 1930 to 1945, a wide variety of investigations confirmed that the primary cosmic rays are mostly protons, and the secondary radiation produced in the atmosphere is primarily electrons, photons and\n       <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">\n        muons\n       </a>\n       . In 1948, observations with nuclear emulsions carried by balloons to near the top of the atmosphere showed that approximately 10% of the primaries are helium nuclei (\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_particle" title="Alpha particle">\n        alpha particles\n       </a>\n       ) and 1% are heavier nuclei of the elements such as carbon, iron, and lead.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freier-1948_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-freier-1948-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freier-1948b_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-freier-1948b-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During a test of his equipment for measuring the east-west effect, Rossi observed that the rate of near-simultaneous discharges of two widely separated\n       <a href="/wiki/Geiger_counter" title="Geiger counter">\n        Geiger counters\n       </a>\n       was larger than the expected accidental rate. In his report on the experiment, Rossi wrote "...\xc2\xa0it seems that once in a while the recording equipment is struck by very extensive showers of particles, which causes coincidences between the counters, even placed at large distances from one another."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rossi-1934b_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rossi-1934b-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1937\n       <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Victor_Auger" title="Pierre Victor Auger">\n        Pierre Auger\n       </a>\n       , unaware of Rossi\'s earlier report, detected the same phenomenon and investigated it in some detail. He concluded that high-energy primary cosmic-ray particles interact with air nuclei high in the atmosphere, initiating a cascade of secondary interactions that ultimately yield a shower of electrons, and photons that reach ground level.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rmp11_3_4_288_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rmp11_3_4_288-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Soviet physicist Sergey Vernov was the first to use\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiosonde" title="Radiosonde">\n        radiosondes\n       </a>\n       to perform cosmic ray readings with an instrument carried to high altitude by a balloon. On 1 April 1935, he took measurements at heights up to 13.6 kilometers using a pair of\n       <a href="/wiki/Geiger_counter" title="Geiger counter">\n        Geiger counters\n       </a>\n       in an anti-coincidence circuit to avoid counting secondary ray showers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Homi_J._Bhabha" title="Homi J. Bhabha">\n        Homi J. Bhabha\n       </a>\n       derived an expression for the probability of scattering positrons by electrons, a process now known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Bhabha_scattering" title="Bhabha scattering">\n        Bhabha scattering\n       </a>\n       . His classic paper, jointly with\n       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Heitler" title="Walter Heitler">\n        Walter Heitler\n       </a>\n       , published in 1937 described how primary cosmic rays from space interact with the upper atmosphere to produce particles observed at the ground level. Bhabha and Heitler explained the cosmic ray shower formation by the cascade production of gamma rays and positive and negative electron pairs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BhabhaHeitler1937_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BhabhaHeitler1937-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_distribution">\n        Energy distribution\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Energy distribution">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Measurements of the energy and arrival directions of the ultra-high energy primary cosmic rays by the techniques of\n       <i>\n        density sampling\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        fast timing\n       </i>\n       of extensive air showers were first carried out in 1954 by members of the Rossi Cosmic Ray Group at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">\n        Massachusetts Institute of Technology\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rossi-1961_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rossi-1961-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The experiment employed eleven\n       <a href="/wiki/Scintillator" title="Scintillator">\n        scintillation detectors\n       </a>\n       arranged within a circle 460 meters in diameter on the grounds of the Agassiz Station of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Harvard_College_Observatory" title="Harvard College Observatory">\n        Harvard College Observatory\n       </a>\n       . From that work, and from many other experiments carried out all over the world, the energy spectrum of the primary cosmic rays is now known to extend beyond 10\n       <sup>\n        20\n       </sup>\n       eV. A huge air shower experiment called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Auger_Observatory" title="Pierre Auger Observatory">\n        Auger Project\n       </a>\n       is currently operated at a site on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pampa" title="Pampa">\n        pampas\n       </a>\n       of Argentina by an international consortium of physicists, led by\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Cronin" title="James Cronin">\n        James Cronin\n       </a>\n       , winner of the 1980\n       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">\n        Nobel Prize in Physics\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">\n        University of Chicago\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Andrew_Watson" title="Alan Andrew Watson">\n        Alan Watson\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">\n        University of Leeds\n       </a>\n       . Their aim is to explore the properties and arrival directions of the very highest-energy primary cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auger-website_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-auger-website-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The results are expected to have important implications for particle physics and cosmology, due to a theoretical\n       <a href="/wiki/Greisen%E2%80%93Zatsepin%E2%80%93Kuzmin_limit" title="Greisen\xe2\x80\x93Zatsepin\xe2\x80\x93Kuzmin limit">\n        Greisen\xe2\x80\x93Zatsepin\xe2\x80\x93Kuzmin limit\n       </a>\n       to the energies of cosmic rays from long distances (about 160 million light years) which occurs above 10\n       <sup>\n        20\n       </sup>\n       eV because of interactions with the remnant photons from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">\n        Big Bang\n       </a>\n       origin of the universe.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       High-energy gamma rays (&gt;50\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       MeV photons) were finally discovered in the primary cosmic radiation by an MIT experiment carried on the OSO-3 satellite in 1967.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kraushaar-1972_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-kraushaar-1972-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Components of both galactic and extra-galactic origins were separately identified at intensities much less than 1% of the primary charged particles. Since then, numerous satellite gamma-ray observatories have mapped the gamma-ray sky. The most recent is the Fermi Observatory, which has produced a map showing a narrow band of gamma ray intensity produced in discrete and diffuse sources in our galaxy, and numerous point-like extra-galactic sources distributed over the celestial sphere.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sources_of_cosmic_rays">\n        Sources of cosmic rays\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sources of cosmic rays">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Early speculation on the sources of cosmic rays included a 1934 proposal by Baade and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Zwicky" title="Fritz Zwicky">\n        Zwicky\n       </a>\n       suggesting cosmic rays originated from supernovae.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaadeZwicky1934_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BaadeZwicky1934-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 1948 proposal by\n       <a href="/wiki/Horace_W._Babcock" title="Horace W. Babcock">\n        Horace W. Babcock\n       </a>\n       suggested that magnetic variable stars could be a source of cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-babcock-1948_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-babcock-1948-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Subsequently, in 1951, Y. Sekido\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       identified the\n       <a href="/wiki/Crab_Nebula" title="Crab Nebula">\n        Crab Nebula\n       </a>\n       as a source of cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sediko-1951_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sediko-1951-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since then, a wide variety of potential sources for cosmic rays began to surface, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">\n        supernovae\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_galactic_nuclei" title="Active galactic nuclei">\n        active galactic nuclei\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Quasar" title="Quasar">\n        quasars\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_burst" title="Gamma-ray burst">\n        gamma-ray bursts\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cosmicraysources_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cosmicraysources-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="546" data-file-width="824" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg/220px-PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg/330px-PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg/440px-PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA16938-RadiationSources-InterplanetarySpace.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sources of ionizing radiation in interplanetary space.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Later experiments have helped to identify the sources of cosmic rays with greater certainty. In 2009, a paper presented at the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Cosmic_Ray_Conference" title="International Cosmic Ray Conference">\n        International Cosmic Ray Conference\n       </a>\n       (ICRC) by scientists at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Auger_Observatory" title="Pierre Auger Observatory">\n        Pierre Auger Observatory\n       </a>\n       showed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultra-high_energy_cosmic_ray" title="Ultra-high energy cosmic ray">\n        ultra-high energy cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       (UHECRs) originating from a location in the sky very close to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Radio_galaxy" title="Radio galaxy">\n        radio galaxy\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Centaurus_A" title="Centaurus A">\n        Centaurus A\n       </a>\n       , although the authors specifically stated that further investigation would be required to confirm Cen A as a source of cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auger-2009-1_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-auger-2009-1-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, no correlation was found between the incidence of gamma-ray bursts and cosmic rays, causing the authors to set upper limits as low as 3.4\xc2\xa0\xc3\x97\xc2\xa010\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x926\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Erg" title="Erg">\n        erg\n       </a>\n       \xc2\xb7cm\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x922\n       </sup>\n       on the flux of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        1 GeV \xe2\x80\x93 1 TeV\n       </span>\n       cosmic rays from gamma-ray bursts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auger-2009-2_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-auger-2009-2-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2009, supernovae were said to have been "pinned down" as a source of cosmic rays, a discovery made by a group using data from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Very_Large_Telescope" title="Very Large Telescope">\n        Very Large Telescope\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moskowitz-2009_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-moskowitz-2009-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This analysis, however, was disputed in 2011 with data from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_for_Antimatter_Matter_Exploration_and_Light-nuclei_Astrophysics" title="Payload for Antimatter Matter Exploration and Light-nuclei Astrophysics">\n        PAMELA\n       </a>\n       , which revealed that "spectral shapes of [hydrogen and helium nuclei] are different and cannot be described well by a single power law", suggesting a more complex process of cosmic ray formation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-piccoza-2011_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-piccoza-2011-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In February 2013, though, research analyzing data from\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fermi_Gamma-ray_Space_Telescope" title="Fermi Gamma-ray Space Telescope">\n         Fermi\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       revealed through an observation of neutral pion decay that supernovae were indeed a source of cosmic rays, with each explosion producing roughly 3\xc2\xa0\xc3\x97\xc2\xa010\n       <sup>\n        42\n       </sup>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 3\xc2\xa0\xc3\x97\xc2\xa010\n       <sup>\n        43\n       </sup>\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">\n        J\n       </a>\n       of cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ackermann-2013_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ackermann-2013-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinholster-2013_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pinholster-2013-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, supernovae do not produce all cosmic rays, and the proportion of cosmic rays that they do produce is a question which cannot be answered without further study.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jha-2013_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jha-2013-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2017, a research paper used data from the International Space Station identified a possible source as dark matter being "a self-annihilating WIMP".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Types">\n        Types\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Types">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays can be divided into two types,\n       <b>\n        galactic cosmic rays\n       </b>\n       (\n       <b>\n        GCR\n       </b>\n       ), high energy particles originating outside the solar system, and\n       <b>\n        <a href="/wiki/Solar_energetic_particles" title="Solar energetic particles">\n         solar energetic particles\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       , high energy particles (predominantly protons) emitted by the sun, primarily in\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_particle_event" title="Solar particle event">\n        solar particle events\n       </a>\n       . However, the term "cosmic ray" is often used to refer to only the GCR flux. Despite the nomenclature\n       <i>\n        galactic\n       </i>\n       , GCRs may originate within or outside the galaxy (as discussed in the source section above).\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atmospheric_Collision.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="419" data-file-width="850" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Atmospheric_Collision.svg/400px-Atmospheric_Collision.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Atmospheric_Collision.svg/600px-Atmospheric_Collision.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Atmospheric_Collision.svg/800px-Atmospheric_Collision.svg.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atmospheric_Collision.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Primary cosmic particle collides with a molecule of atmosphere.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays originate as primary cosmic rays, which are those originally produced in various astrophysical processes. Primary cosmic rays are composed primarily of protons and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_particle" title="Alpha particle">\n        alpha particles\n       </a>\n       (99%), with a small amount of heavier nuclei (~1%) and an extremely minute proportion of\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Antiproton" title="Antiproton">\n        antiprotons\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goddard-2012_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-goddard-2012-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Secondary cosmic rays, caused by a decay of primary cosmic rays as they impact an atmosphere, include\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">\n        neutrons\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pion" title="Pion">\n        pions\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">\n        muons\n       </a>\n       . Of these four, the latter three were first detected in cosmic rays.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_cosmic_rays">\n        Primary cosmic rays\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Primary cosmic rays">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Primary cosmic rays primarily originate from outside the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">\n        Solar system\n       </a>\n       and sometimes even the\n       <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">\n        Milky Way\n       </a>\n       . When they interact with Earth\'s atmosphere, they are converted to secondary particles. The mass ratio of helium to hydrogen nuclei, 28%, is similar to the primordial\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elemental_abundance" title="Elemental abundance">\n        elemental abundance\n       </a>\n       ratio of these elements, 24%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The remaining fraction is made up of the other heavier nuclei that are typical nucleosynthesis end products, primarily\n       <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">\n        lithium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Beryllium" title="Beryllium">\n        beryllium\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boron" title="Boron">\n        boron\n       </a>\n       . These nuclei appear in cosmic rays in much greater abundance (~1%) than in the solar atmosphere, where they are only about 10\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x9211\n       </sup>\n       as abundant as\n       <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">\n        helium\n       </a>\n       . Cosmic rays made up of charged nuclei heavier than helium are called\n       <a href="/wiki/HZE_ions" title="HZE ions">\n        HZE ions\n       </a>\n       . Due to the high charge and heavy nature of HZE ions, their contribution to an astronaut\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiation_dose" title="Radiation dose">\n        radiation dose\n       </a>\n       in space is significant even though they are relatively scarce.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This abundance difference is a result of the way secondary cosmic rays are formed. Carbon and oxygen nuclei collide with interstellar matter to form\n       <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">\n        lithium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Beryllium" title="Beryllium">\n        beryllium\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boron" title="Boron">\n        boron\n       </a>\n       in a process termed\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray_spallation" title="Cosmic ray spallation">\n        cosmic ray spallation\n       </a>\n       . Spallation is also responsible for the abundances of\n       <a href="/wiki/Scandium" title="Scandium">\n        scandium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">\n        titanium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vanadium" title="Vanadium">\n        vanadium\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">\n        manganese\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ion" title="Ion">\n        ions\n       </a>\n       in cosmic rays produced by collisions of iron and nickel nuclei with\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_medium" title="Interstellar medium">\n        interstellar matter\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-koch-2012_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-koch-2012-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_cosmic_ray_antimatter">\n        Primary cosmic ray antimatter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Primary cosmic ray antimatter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer" title="Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer">\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Satellite experiments have found evidence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       and a few antiprotons in primary cosmic rays, amounting to less than 1% of the particles in primary cosmic rays. These do not appear to be the products of large amounts of antimatter from the Big Bang, or indeed complex antimatter in the universe. Rather, they appear to consist of only these two elementary particles, newly made in energetic processes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Preliminary results from the presently operating\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer" title="Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer">\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        AMS-02\n       </i>\n       ) on board the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       show that positrons in the cosmic rays arrive with no directionality, and with energies that range from 10\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gigaelectron_volt" title="wiktionary:gigaelectron volt">\n        GeV\n       </a>\n       to 250\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       GeV. In September, 2014, new results with almost twice as much data were presented in a talk at CERN and published in Physical Review Letters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A new measurement of positron fraction up to 500 GeV was reported, showing that positron fraction peaks at a maximum of about 16% of total electron+positron events, around an energy of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        275\xc2\xb132 GeV\n       </span>\n       . At higher energies, up to 500\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       GeV, the ratio of positrons to electrons begins to fall again. The absolute flux of positrons also begins to fall before 500\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       GeV, but peaks at energies far higher than electron energies, which peak about 10\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       GeV.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These results on interpretation have been suggested to be due to positron production in annihilation events of massive\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">\n        dark matter\n       </a>\n       particles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-physrevltrs413_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-physrevltrs413-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic ray antiprotons also have a much higher average energy than their normal-matter counterparts (protons). They arrive at Earth with a characteristic energy maximum of 2\xc2\xa0GeV, indicating their production in a fundamentally different process from cosmic ray protons, which on average have only one-sixth of the energy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is no evidence of complex antimatter atomic nuclei, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antihelium" title="Antihelium">\n        antihelium\n       </a>\n       nuclei (i.e., anti-alpha particles), in cosmic rays. These are actively being searched for. A prototype of the\n       <i>\n        AMS-02\n       </i>\n       designated\n       <i>\n        AMS-01\n       </i>\n       , was flown into space aboard the\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-91" title="STS-91">\n        STS-91\n       </a>\n       in June 1998. By not detecting any\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antihelium#Antihelium" title="Antihelium">\n        antihelium\n       </a>\n       at all, the\n       <i>\n        AMS-01\n       </i>\n       established an upper limit of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        1.1 \xc3\x97 10\n        <sup>\n         \xe2\x88\x926\n        </sup>\n       </span>\n       for the antihelium to helium\n       <a href="/wiki/Flux" title="Flux">\n        flux\n       </a>\n       ratio.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">\n        <div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">\n         The moon in cosmic rays\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon%27s_shadow_in_muons.gif">\n           <img alt="The moon\'s muon shadow" data-file-height="273" data-file-width="367" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Moon%27s_shadow_in_muons.gif/200px-Moon%27s_shadow_in_muons.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Moon%27s_shadow_in_muons.gif/300px-Moon%27s_shadow_in_muons.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/6f/Moon%27s_shadow_in_muons.gif 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          The\n          <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n           Moon\n          </a>\n          \'s cosmic ray shadow, as seen in secondary muons detected 700 m below ground, at the\n          <a href="/wiki/Soudan_2" title="Soudan 2">\n           Soudan\xc2\xa02\n          </a>\n          detector\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon_egret.jpg">\n           <img alt="The moon as seen in gamma rays" data-file-height="362" data-file-width="360" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moon_egret.jpg/200px-Moon_egret.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moon_egret.jpg/300px-Moon_egret.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Moon_egret.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          The Moon as seen by the\n          <a href="/wiki/Compton_Gamma_Ray_Observatory" title="Compton Gamma Ray Observatory">\n           Compton Gamma Ray Observatory\n          </a>\n          , in gamma rays with energies greater than 20\xc2\xa0MeV. These are produced by cosmic ray bombardment on its surface.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n           <a href="#cite_note-58">\n            [58]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_cosmic_rays">\n        Secondary cosmic rays\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Secondary cosmic rays">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       When cosmic rays enter the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth\'s atmosphere">\n        Earth\'s atmosphere\n       </a>\n       they collide with\n       <a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">\n        atoms\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecules\n       </a>\n       , mainly oxygen and nitrogen. The interaction produces a cascade of lighter particles, a so-called\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_shower_(physics)" title="Air shower (physics)">\n        air shower\n       </a>\n       secondary radiation that rains down, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-rays" title="X-rays">\n        x-rays\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">\n        muons\n       </a>\n       , protons,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_particle" title="Alpha particle">\n        alpha particles\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pion" title="Pion">\n        pions\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">\n        electrons\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">\n        neutrons\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All of the produced particles stay within about one degree of the primary particle\'s path.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Typical particles produced in such collisions are\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">\n        neutrons\n       </a>\n       and charged\n       <a href="/wiki/Meson" title="Meson">\n        mesons\n       </a>\n       such as positive or negative\n       <a href="/wiki/Pion" title="Pion">\n        pions\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Kaon" title="Kaon">\n        kaons\n       </a>\n       . Some of these subsequently decay into\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muons" title="Muons">\n        muons\n       </a>\n       , which are able to reach the surface of the Earth, and even penetrate for some distance into shallow mines. The muons can be easily detected by many types of particle detectors, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Cloud_chamber" title="Cloud chamber">\n        cloud chambers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bubble_chamber" title="Bubble chamber">\n        bubble chambers\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Scintillation_(physics)" title="Scintillation (physics)">\n        scintillation\n       </a>\n       detectors. The observation of a secondary shower of particles in multiple detectors at the same time is an indication that all of the particles came from that event.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays impacting other planetary bodies in the Solar System are detected indirectly by observing high energy\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n        gamma ray\n       </a>\n       emissions by gamma-ray telescope. These are distinguished from radioactive decay processes by their higher energies above \xc2\xa0about 10\xc2\xa0MeV.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cosmic-ray_flux">\n        Cosmic-ray flux\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cosmic-ray flux">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1453" data-file-width="3175" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg/400px-SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg/600px-SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg/800px-SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpaceEnvironmentOverview_From_19830101.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         An overview of the space environment shows the relationship between the solar activity and galactic cosmic rays.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n          <a href="#cite_note-60">\n           [60]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Flux" title="Flux">\n        flux\n       </a>\n       of incoming cosmic rays at the upper atmosphere is dependent on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">\n        solar wind\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field" title="Earth\'s magnetic field">\n        Earth\'s magnetic field\n       </a>\n       , and the energy of the cosmic rays. At distances of ~94\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">\n        AU\n       </a>\n       from the Sun, the solar wind undergoes a transition, called the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Termination_shock" title="Termination shock">\n        termination shock\n       </a>\n       , from supersonic to subsonic speeds. The region between the termination shock and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heliopause_(astronomy)" title="Heliopause (astronomy)">\n        heliopause\n       </a>\n       acts as a barrier to cosmic rays, decreasing the flux at lower energies (\xe2\x89\xa4\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       1\xc2\xa0GeV) by about\xc2\xa090%. However, the strength of the solar wind is not constant, and hence it has been observed that cosmic ray flux is correlated with solar activity.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, the Earth\'s magnetic field acts to deflect cosmic rays from its surface, giving rise to the observation that the flux is apparently dependent on\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitude\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">\n        longitude\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Azimuth" title="Azimuth">\n        azimuth angle\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The combined effects of all of the factors mentioned contribute to the flux of cosmic rays at Earth\'s surface. The following table of participial frequencies reach the planet\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and are inferred from lower energy radiation reaching the ground\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Particle energy (eV)\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Particle rate (m\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x88\x922\n         </sup>\n         s\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x88\x921\n         </sup>\n         )\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           7009100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           9\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         (GeV)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           7004100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           4\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           7012100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           12\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         (TeV)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           7016100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           16\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         (10\n         <span class="nowrap">\n         </span>\n         PeV)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           6993100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           \xe2\x88\x927\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         (a few times a year)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           7020100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           20\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         (100\n         <span class="nowrap">\n         </span>\n         EeV)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n           6985100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n          </span>\n          1\n          <span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">\n           \xc3\x97\n          </span>\n          10\n          <sup>\n           \xe2\x88\x9215\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         (once a
