century)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       In the past, it was believed that the cosmic ray flux remained fairly constant over time. However, recent research suggests 1.5 to 2-fold millennium-timescale changes in the cosmic ray flux in the past forty thousand years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The magnitude of the energy of cosmic ray flux in interstellar space is very comparable to that of other deep space energies: cosmic ray energy density averages about one electron-volt per cubic centimeter of interstellar space, or ~1\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       eV/cm\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       , which is comparable to the energy density of visible starlight at 0.3\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       eV/cm\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galactic_magnetic_fields" title="Galactic magnetic fields">\n        galactic magnetic field\n       </a>\n       energy density (assumed 3 microgauss) which is ~0.25\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       eV/cm\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       , or the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background" title="Cosmic microwave background">\n        cosmic microwave background\n       </a>\n       (CMB) radiation energy density at ~ 0.25\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       eV/cm\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Detection_methods">\n        Detection methods\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Detection methods">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VERITAS_array.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="955" data-file-width="2678" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/VERITAS_array.jpg/600px-VERITAS_array.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/VERITAS_array.jpg/900px-VERITAS_array.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/VERITAS_array.jpg/1200px-VERITAS_array.jpg 2x" width="600"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VERITAS_array.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/VERITAS" title="VERITAS">\n          VERITAS\n         </a>\n         array of air Cherenkov telescopes.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There are several ground-based methods of detecting cosmic rays currently in use. The first detection method is called the air Cherenkov telescope, designed to detect low-energy (&lt;200\xc2\xa0GeV) cosmic rays by means of analyzing their\n       <a href="/wiki/Cherenkov_radiation" title="Cherenkov radiation">\n        Cherenkov radiation\n       </a>\n       , which for cosmic rays are gamma rays emitted as they travel faster than the\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">\n        speed of light\n       </a>\n       in their medium, the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-losalamos-2002_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-losalamos-2002-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While these telescopes are extremely good at distinguishing between background radiation and that of cosmic-ray origin, they can only function well on clear nights without the Moon shining, and have very small fields of view and are only active for a few percent of the time. Another Cherenkov telescope uses water as a medium through which particles pass and produce Cherenkov radiation to make them detectable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michiganstate_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-michiganstate-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1017" data-file-width="900" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/250px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/375px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png/500px-PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA17601-Comparisons-RadiationExposure-MarsTrip-20131209.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Comparison of radiation doses, including the amount detected on the trip from Earth to Mars by the\n         <a href="/wiki/Radiation_assessment_detector" title="Radiation assessment detector">\n          RAD\n         </a>\n         on the\n         <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n          MSL\n         </a>\n         (2011 \xe2\x80\x93 2013).\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531a_19-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531a-19">\n           [19]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20130531b_20-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20130531b-20">\n           [20]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20130530_21-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130530-21">\n           [21]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Extensive air shower (EAS) arrays, a second detection method, measure the charged particles which pass through them. EAS arrays measure much higher-energy cosmic rays than air Cherenkov telescopes, and can observe a broad area of the sky and can be active about 90% of the time. However, they are less able to segregate background effects from cosmic rays than can air Cherenkov telescopes. EAS arrays employ plastic\n       <a href="/wiki/Scintillator" title="Scintillator">\n        scintillators\n       </a>\n       in order to detect particles.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another method was developed by Robert Fleischer,\n       <a href="/wiki/P._Buford_Price" title="P. Buford Price">\n        P.\xc2\xa0Buford Price\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_M._Walker_(physicist)" title="Robert M. Walker (physicist)">\n        Robert\xc2\xa0M. Walker\n       </a>\n       for use in high-altitude balloons.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FPW_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FPW-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In this method, sheets of clear plastic, like 0.25\n       <a href="/wiki/Millimetre" title="Millimetre">\n        mm\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lexan" title="Lexan">\n        Lexan\n       </a>\n       polycarbonate, are stacked together and exposed directly to cosmic rays in space or high altitude. The nuclear charge causes chemical bond breaking or\n       <a href="/wiki/Ionization" title="Ionization">\n        ionization\n       </a>\n       in the plastic. At the top of the plastic stack the ionization is less, due to the high cosmic ray speed. As the cosmic ray speed decreases due to deceleration in the stack, the ionization increases along the path. The resulting plastic sheets are "etched" or slowly dissolved in warm caustic\n       <a href="/wiki/Sodium_hydroxide" title="Sodium hydroxide">\n        sodium hydroxide\n       </a>\n       solution, that removes the surface material at a slow, known rate. The caustic sodium hydroxide dissolves the plastic at a faster rate along the path of the ionized plastic. The net result is a conical etch pit in the plastic. The etch pits are measured under a high-power microscope (typically 1600\xc3\x97 oil-immersion), and the etch rate is plotted as a function of the depth in the stacked plastic.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This technique yields a unique curve for each atomic nucleus from 1 to\xc2\xa092, allowing identification of both the charge and energy of the cosmic ray that traverses the plastic stack. The more extensive the ionization along the path, the higher the charge. In addition to its uses for cosmic-ray detection, the technique is also used to detect nuclei created as products of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">\n        nuclear fission\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A fourth method involves the use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cloud_chamber" title="Cloud chamber">\n        cloud chambers\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chess-2006_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-chess-2006-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to detect the secondary muons created when a pion decays. Cloud chambers in particular can be built from widely available materials and can be constructed even in a high-school laboratory. A fifth method, involving\n       <a href="/wiki/Bubble_chamber" title="Bubble chamber">\n        bubble chambers\n       </a>\n       , can be used to detect cosmic ray particles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chu-1970_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-chu-1970-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another method detects the light from nitrogen fluorescence caused by the excitation of nitrogen in the atmosphere by the shower of particles moving through the atmosphere. This method allows for accurate detection of the direction from which the cosmic ray came.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Finally, the\n       <a href="/wiki/CMOS" title="CMOS">\n        CMOS\n       </a>\n       devices in pervasive\n       <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">\n        smartphone\n       </a>\n       cameras have been proposed as a practical distributed network to detect air showers from ultra-high energy cosmic rays (UHECRs) which is at least comparable with that of conventional cosmic ray detectors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">\n        app\n       </a>\n       , which is currently in beta and accepting applications, is CRAYFIS (Cosmic RAYs Found In Smartphones).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">\n        Effects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Effects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_in_atmospheric_chemistry">\n        Changes in atmospheric chemistry\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Changes in atmospheric chemistry">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays ionize the nitrogen and oxygen molecules in the atmosphere, which leads to a number of chemical reactions. One of the reactions results in ozone depletion. Cosmic rays are also responsible for the continuous production of a number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Radionuclide" title="Radionuclide">\n        unstable isotopes\n       </a>\n       in the Earth\'s atmosphere, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">\n        carbon-14\n       </a>\n       , via the reaction:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        n +\n        <sup>\n         14\n        </sup>\n        N \xe2\x86\x92 p +\n        <sup>\n         14\n        </sup>\n        C\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays kept the level of\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">\n        carbon-14\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trumbore_2000_41.E2.80.9359_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trumbore_2000_41.E2.80.9359-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in the atmosphere roughly constant (70 tons) for at least the past 100,000 years,\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       until the beginning of above-ground nuclear weapons testing in the early 1950s. This is an important fact used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">\n        radiocarbon dating\n       </a>\n       used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">\n        archaeology\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Reaction products of primary cosmic rays, radioisotope half-lifetime, and production reaction.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n         <a href="#cite_note-75">\n          [75]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n       <ul>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium">\n          Tritium\n         </a>\n         (12.3 years):\n         <sup>\n          14\n         </sup>\n         N(n,\n         <sup>\n          3\n         </sup>\n         H)\n         <sup>\n          12\n         </sup>\n         C (\n         <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray_spallation" title="Cosmic ray spallation">\n          spallation\n         </a>\n         )\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Beryllium-7 (53.3 days)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Beryllium-10" title="Beryllium-10">\n          Beryllium-10\n         </a>\n         (1.39 million years):\n         <sup>\n          14\n         </sup>\n         N(n,p \xce\xb1)\n         <sup>\n          10\n         </sup>\n         Be (spallation)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">\n          Carbon-14\n         </a>\n         (5730 years):\n         <sup>\n          14\n         </sup>\n         N(n, p)\n         <sup>\n          14\n         </sup>\n         C (\n         <a href="/wiki/Neutron_activation" title="Neutron activation">\n          neutron activation\n         </a>\n         )\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Sodium-22 (2.6 years)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Sodium-24 (15 hours)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Magnesium-28 (20.9 hours)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Silicon-31 (2.6 hours)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Silicon-32 (101 years)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Phosphorus-32 (14.3 days)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Sulfur-35 (87.5 days)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Sulfur-38 (2.84 hours)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Chlorine-34 m (32 minutes)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Chlorine-36" title="Chlorine-36">\n          Chlorine-36\n         </a>\n         (300,000 years)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Chlorine-38 (37.2 minutes)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Chlorine-39 (56 minutes)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Argon-39 (269 years)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Krypton-85 (10.7 years)\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_ambient_radiation">\n        Role in ambient radiation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Role in ambient radiation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays constitute a fraction of the annual radiation exposure of human beings on the Earth, averaging 0.39\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       mSv out of a total of 3\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       mSv per year (13% of total background) for the Earth\'s population. However, the background radiation from cosmic rays increases with altitude, from 0.3\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       mSv per year for sea-level areas to 1.0\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       mSv per year for higher-altitude cities, raising cosmic radiation exposure to a quarter of total background radiation exposure for populations of said cities. Airline crews flying long distance high-altitude routes can be exposed to 2.2\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       mSv of extra radiation each year due to cosmic rays, nearly doubling their total ionizing radiation exposure.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n       <caption>\n        Average annual radiation exposure (\n        <a 6.20\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3.61\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3.81\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <small>\n         Figures are for the time before the\n         <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">\n          Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster\n         </a>\n         . Human-made values by UNSCEAR are from the Japanese National Institute of Radiological Sciences, which summarized the UNSCEAR data.\n        </small>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_electronics">\n        Effect on electronics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Effect on electronics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays have sufficient energy to alter the states of circuit components in\n       <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">\n        electronic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">\n        integrated circuits\n       </a>\n       , causing transient errors to occur (such as corrupted data in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Random_access_memory" title="Random access memory">\n        electronic memory devices\n       </a>\n       or incorrect performance of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPU" title="CPU">\n        CPUs\n       </a>\n       ) often referred to as "\n       <a href="/wiki/Soft_error" title="Soft error">\n        soft errors\n       </a>\n       ." This has been a problem in\n       <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">\n        electronics\n       </a>\n       at extremely high-altitude, such as in\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">\n        satellites\n       </a>\n       , but with\n       <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">\n        transistors\n       </a>\n       becoming smaller and smaller, this is becoming an increasing concern in ground-level electronics as well.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Studies by\n       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">\n        IBM\n       </a>\n       in the 1990s suggest that computers typically experience about one cosmic-ray-induced error per 256 megabytes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Random-access_memory" title="Random-access memory">\n        RAM\n       </a>\n       per month.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       To alleviate this problem, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" title="Intel Corporation">\n        Intel Corporation\n       </a>\n       has proposed a cosmic ray detector that could be integrated into future high-density\n       <a href="/wiki/Microprocessor" title="Microprocessor">\n        microprocessors\n       </a>\n       , allowing the processor to repeat the last command following a cosmic-ray event.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays were suspected as a possible cause of an in-flight incident in 2008 where an\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">\n        Airbus A330\n       </a>\n       airliner of\n       <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">\n        Qantas\n       </a>\n       twice\n       <a href="/wiki/Qantas_Flight_72" title="Qantas Flight 72">\n        plunged hundreds of feet\n       </a>\n       after an unexplained malfunction in its flight control system. Many passengers and crew members were injured, some seriously. After this incident, the accident investigators for NW Australia gave the ruling that, "there was a design flaw in the air data inertial reference unit and a limitation of the aircraft\'s computer software. The serious Qantas A330 upset was caused by a long dormant computer flaw triggered by chance."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This has prompted a software upgrade to all A330 and A340 airliners, worldwide, so that any data spikes in this system are filtered out electronically.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation_hardening" title="Radiation hardening">\n        radiation hardening\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/ECC_memory" title="ECC memory">\n        ECC memory\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Significance_to_aerospace_travel">\n        Significance to aerospace travel\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Significance to aerospace travel">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Health_threat_from_cosmic_rays" title="Health threat from cosmic rays">\n        Health threat from cosmic rays\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Galactic cosmic rays are one of the most important barriers standing in the way of plans for interplanetary travel by crewed spacecraft. Cosmic rays also pose a threat to electronics placed aboard outgoing probes. In 2010, a malfunction aboard the\n       <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">\n        Voyager 2\n       </a>\n       space probe was credited to a single flipped bit, probably caused by a cosmic ray. Strategies such as physical or magnetic shielding for spacecraft have been considered in order to minimize the damage to electronics and human beings caused by cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globus-2002_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-globus-2002-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atkinson-2005_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atkinson-2005-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Flying 12 kilometres (39,000\xc2\xa0ft) high, passengers and crews of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_airliner" title="Jet airliner">\n        jet airliners\n       </a>\n       are exposed to at least 10 times the cosmic ray dose that people at\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">\n        sea level\n       </a>\n       receive. Aircraft flying\n       <a href="/wiki/Polar_route" title="Polar route">\n        polar routes\n       </a>\n       near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Geomagnetic_pole" title="Geomagnetic pole">\n        geomagnetic poles\n       </a>\n       are at particular risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_lightning">\n        Role in lightning\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Role in lightning">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Cosmic rays have been implicated in the triggering of electrical breakdown in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       . It has been proposed that essentially all lightning is triggered through a relativistic process, "\n       <a href="/wiki/Runaway_breakdown" title="Runaway breakdown">\n        runaway breakdown\n       </a>\n       ", seeded by cosmic ray secondaries. Subsequent development of the lightning discharge then occurs through "conventional breakdown" mechanisms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Postulated_role_in_climate_change">\n        Postulated role in climate change\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Postulated role in climate change">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A role of cosmic rays directly or via solar-induced modulations in climate change was suggested by\n       <a href="/wiki/Edward_P._Ney" title="Edward P. Ney">\n        Edward P. Ney\n       </a>\n       in 1959\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NATURE_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NATURE-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and by\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Dickinson" title="Robert E. Dickinson">\n        Robert E. Dickinson\n       </a>\n       in 1975.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dickinson-1975_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dickinson-1975-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The idea has been revived in recent years, most notably by\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Svensmark" title="Henrik Svensmark">\n        Henrik Svensmark\n       </a>\n       , who has argued that because\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_variation" title="Solar variation">\n        solar variation\n       </a>\n       modulates the cosmic ray flux on Earth, they would consequently affect the rate of cloud formation and hence the climate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, other scientists have vigorously criticized Svensmark for sloppy and inconsistent work: one example is adjustment of cloud data that understates error in lower cloud data, but not in high cloud data;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       another example is "incorrect handling of the physical data" resulting in graphs that do not show the correlations they claim to show.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In any case, 97% of climate scientists\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       support the conclusions in the 2007 IPCC synthesis report, which strongly attributes a major role in the ongoing global warming to human-produced gases such as carbon dioxide, methane, nitrous oxide, and halocarbons, and has stated that models including natural forcings only (including aerosol forcings, which cosmic rays are considered by some to contribute to) would result in far less warming than has actually been observed or predicted in models including anthropogenic forcings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC-2007_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC-2007-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Svensmark is one of several scientists\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_scientists_opposing_the_mainstream_scientific_assessment_of_global_warming" title="List of scientists opposing the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming">\n        outspokenly opposed to the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming\n       </a>\n       . His estimates on the magnitude of the effect of GCR (galactic cosmic rays) on global warming continue to be refuted in the mainstream scientific press.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For instance, a November 2013 study showed that less than 14 percent of global warming since the 1950s could be attributed to cosmic ray rate, and while the models showed a small correlation every 22 years, the cosmic ray rate did not match the changes in temperature, indicating that it was not a causal relationship.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another 2013 study found, contrary to Svensmark\'s claims, "no statistically significant correlations between cosmic rays and global albedo or globally averaged cloud height."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It has also been postulated that cosmic rays may have been responsible for major climatic change and mass-extinction in the past. According to Adrian Mellott and Mikhail Medvedev, 62 million year cycles in biological marine populations correlate with the motion of the earth relative to the galactic plane and increases in exposure to cosmic rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The researchers suggest that this and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n        gamma ray\n       </a>\n       bombardments deriving from local\n       <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">\n        supernovae\n       </a>\n       could have affected\n       <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">\n        cancer\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mutation_rate" title="Mutation rate">\n        mutation rates\n       </a>\n       , and might be linked to decisive alterations in the Earth\'s climate, and to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">\n        mass-extinctions\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">\n        Ordovician\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_experiments">\n        Research and experiments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmic_ray&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Research and experiments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic-ray_observatory" title="Cosmic-ray observatory">\n        Cosmic-ray observatory\n       </a>\n      </div>\n
